The Ruling on a Trained Dog Eating Prey After Owner's Possession
Ruling on a trained dog eating prey after ownership is established.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and reason for the permissibility of the remainder of the prey when a trained dog eats a piece after the owner's possession, and distinguish it from eating before possession.

Core Idea
After possession, the prey is no longer 'sayd' – the dog's eating does not affect permissibility.

This lesson addresses a common question in hunting with trained dogs: what if the dog eats part of the prey after the hunter has taken it into his possession? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the change in the status of the prey once it is possessed. We will explore the ruling, its proof through analogy, and the crucial condition of the dog's training.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a trained dog eating a piece of the prey after the owner has taken possession (ihraz). The ruling states the remainder is halal (mubah).
The dog must be mu'allam (trained) and not have eaten during the hunt.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The author uses qiyas (analogy) to the case of the owner throwing other food to the dog, which is clearly permissible.
The original case (asl) is the owner giving other food; the new case (far') is giving a piece of the same prey after possession.
3
Analyze the qiyas: determine the illa
The effective cause (illa) is that the prey has ceased to be a hunted animal (sayd) because the owner has taken possession (ihraz).
This illa is clear (jaliyyah) and extracted by tanqih al-manat.
4
Distinguish by counter-example
If the dog eats before possession, the prey remains haram because it is still considered sayd (the jihah al-saydiyyah remains).
Contrast: 'bikhilaf ma idha fa'ala dhalika qabla an yuhrizahu al-malik'.
5
Apply the rule and summarize
The condition for the dog's training is to refrain from eating from the prey while it is in the state of being hunted. Eating after possession does not break this condition.
The resting meat is permissible to eat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اخذا الصيد من المعلم ثم قطع منه قطعة والقاها اليه فاكلها يوكل ما بقى لانه لم يبق صيدا فصار كما اذا القى اليه طعاما غيره وكذا اذا وثب الكلب فاخذه منه واكل منه لانه ما اكل من الصيد والشرط ترك الاكل من الصيد فصار كما اذا فترى شاته بخلاف ما اذا فعل ذلك قبل ان يحرزه المالك لانه بقيت فيه جهة الصيدية

ترجمہ اور اگر شکاری نے کلب معلم کے شکار کو لے لیا پھر اس نے شکار میں سے ایک ٹکڑا کاٹا اور اس کو کتے کے سامنے ڈال یا پس اس نے اس کو کھالیا تو مابقی کھایا جائے گا اس لئے کہ وہ شکار باقی نہیں رہا تو ایسا ہو گیا جبکہ اس نے اس کی طرف کوئی اور کھا نا ڈالا ہو اور ایسے ہی جبکہ کتے نے چھلانگ لگائی پس شکار کو مالک سے لے لیا اور اس میں سے کھا لیا ( تو یہ حلال ہے ) اس لئے کہ اس نے شکار میں سے نہیں کھایا اور شرط شکار میں سے کھانے کو چھوڑ نا تھا پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسے جبکہ کتا ما لک کی بکری کو پھاڑ ڈالے بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ کتے نے یہ کام مالک کے احراز سے پہلے کیا ہو اس لئے کہ شکار میں شکار ہونے کی جہت باقی ہے۔

[كتافي؟] تشریح: جب کتے نے شکار پکڑ لیا اور نہیں کھایا تو وہ حلال ہے ( کمامر ) پھر اگر مالک نے شکار میں سے ایک ٹکڑا کاٹ کر کتے کو دیدیا اور اس نے کھا لیا تو اس سے شکار کی حالت پر کچھ فرق نہیں پڑیگا کیونکہ اب وہ شکار نہیں ہے یہ تو ایسا ہے جیسا کہ مالک اس کو کوئی کھانا ڈالدے اور وہ کھالے بلکہ اگر اس حالت میں کتے نے مالک کے ہاتھ سے شکار چھین کر کچھ کھا لے تب بھی مابقی جائز ہے کیونکہ اب یہ شکار ہے ہی نہیں اور معلم ہونے کی شرط شکار میں سے نہ کھانا تھا جیسے اگر مالک کے احراز سے پہلے ہی کتا شکار میں سے کھالے تو اب اس کو کھانا نہ حلال نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ ابھی شکار ہے۔
And if one takes the prey from the trained dog, then cuts a piece from it and throws it to him and he eats it, what remains is eaten (i.e., is permissible) because it is no longer a prey (sayd), so it becomes as if he threw other food to him. Likewise, if the dog jumps and takes it from him and eats from it, (it is permissible) because he did not eat from the prey, and the condition is to refrain from eating from the prey, so it becomes as if he mangled his sheep – unlike if he did that before the owner has taken possession (ihraz), because the aspect of being a prey remains in it. Translation: And if the hunter took the prey of the trained dog, then he cut a piece from it and placed it in front of the dog and he ate it, then the remainder will be eaten because the prey did not remain; so it became as if he had placed some other food before him. Similarly, if the dog jumped and took the prey from the owner and ate from it, it is halal because he did not eat from the prey, and the condition was to refrain from eating from the prey, so it became as if the dog mangled the owner's sheep – unlike the case if he did this before the owner's possession, because the aspect of being a prey remains in it. [Kutafi?] Commentary: When the dog caught the prey and did not eat it, it is halal (as per the ruling). Then if the owner cut a piece from the prey and gave it to the dog and he ate it, this does not affect the status of the prey at all, because now it is not a prey; it is like the owner throwing some food to him and he eats it. Rather, if in this state the dog snatches the prey from the owner's hand and eats some, even then the remainder is permissible because now it is not a prey at all, and the condition of being trained was not to eat from the prey. For example, if before the owner's possession the dog ate from the prey, then eating it is not halal because it is still a prey.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the book of hunting (Kitab al-Sayd). The author states the general principle: once a trained dog catches the prey and does not eat from it, the prey becomes halal. However, if the owner takes the prey into his possession (ihraz) and then cuts a piece and gives it to the dog, or the dog snatches the prey from the owner's hand and eats some, the remainder of the prey remains halal. The reasoning is that after the owner's possession, the prey is no longer considered 'sayd' (hunted game) – it becomes ordinary property. Therefore, the dog eating from it does not affect its halal status, just as if the owner had given the dog other food or if the dog had attacked the owner's livestock. The condition for the dog being trained (mu'allam) is that it does not eat from the prey while it is in the state of being hunted. Once the prey is possessed, that condition is no longer relevant. However, if the dog eats from the prey before the owner takes possession, the prey is not halal because it still retains the aspect of being hunted (jihah al-saydiyyah). The additional commentary clarifies that even if the dog eats a piece after the owner's possession, the remaining meat is permissible to eat. The key point is the distinction based on ownership (ihraz): before ihraz, the prey is still considered raw game; after ihraz, it is owned meat.

Key Terms
كلب معلم (kalb mu'allam): A dog that has been trained for hunting and has the trait of not eating the prey when commanded.
صيد (sayd): Hunted game animal; in this context, the animal caught by the dog.
احراز (ihraz): Taking possession; the act of the hunter taking the prey into his custody, thereby removing its status as game.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if a trained dog catches a deer and the hunter takes possession of it, then cuts a piece and gives it to the dog, what is the status of the remaining deer meat?
A) It is haram because the dog ate from it.
B) It is halal because the prey is no longer considered 'sayd' after possession.
C) It is makruh because the dog consumed a part.
D) It depends on whether the dog ate the entire piece.

Key Takeaway
The condition for the trained dog is to refrain from eating during the hunt; after the owner possesses the prey, the dog's eating does not affect its permissibility.

Timing of the Dog's Consumption and Its Effect on Prey Permissibility
Ruling on dog that bites, spits, hunts, then eats piece

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between permissible and impermissible scenarios when a trained dog bites a piece of prey and later eats it, by applying the Hanafi principle that eating during hunting indicates ignorance but eating after possession does not.

Core Idea
A dog eating from prey after the owner's possession does not affect permissibility; only eating during the hunt indicates the dog is untrained.

This lesson examines a nuanced scenario in hunting with trained dogs: the dog bites a piece from the prey, spits it out, continues the hunt, and later eats that piece after the owner has taken the prey. At first glance, one might think the prey becomes impermissible because the dog consumed part of it. However, the Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between the dog's actions during the hunt (istiyad) and after the prey is secured (ihraz). Understanding this temporal distinction is essential for correctly applying the rules of lawful hunting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage contrasts two cases: (1) the dog bites a piece and eats it during the chase (previous lesson, prey haram), and (2) the dog bites a piece, spits it out, hunts, and later eats the piece after the owner has taken the prey (current lesson, prey halal).
Both involve the dog eating the same piece; only the timing differs.
2
Determine the dog's intent
Biting a piece can be either to eat it (indicating ignorance/untrained) or as a trick (hilah) to weaken the prey. The timing reveals the intent: eating before capture indicates the first, eating after capture indicates the second.
The dog's state of being jahil (ignorant) is determined by its actions during the hunt.
3
Apply the key principle
In Hanafi fiqh, if a trained dog eats from the prey during the hunt, the prey becomes haram because it shows the dog is untrained. However, if the dog eats after the owner has possessed the prey, it does not affect permissibility, as the dog is no longer in the hunting state.
The principle is derived from the hadith: 'If he eats from it, then do not eat' applies only during the hunt.
4
Reason from the stronger case (qiyas awla)
The text argues: if the dog had eaten from the prey itself after possession, it would not harm permissibility. So eating a detached piece (which is even less connected to the prey) is even less harmful. This is an a fortiori argument.
The detached piece is not halal for the owner to eat (since it was not properly slaughtered), but that does not affect the prey's permissibility.
5
Conclude the ruling
The prey is halal (mubah) in this scenario. The dog's action of spitting out the piece and continuing the chase shows it was a tactic, not ignorance. Eating after possession does not invalidate the hunt.
This ruling is mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو القى ما نهسه واتبع الصيد فقتله ولم ياكل منه واخذه صاحبه ثم مربتلك البضعة فاكلها يوكل الصيد لانه لواكل من نفس الصيد في هذه الحالة لن يضره فاذا اكل ما بان منه وهو لا يحل لصاحبه اولى
ترجمہ اور اگر کتے نے جو ٹکڑا نو چاہے اس کو ڈال دیا اور شکار کا پیچھا کیا پس اس کو قتل کر دیا اور اس میں سے نہیں کھایا اور شکار کو اس کے مالک نے لے لیا پھر سکتا گذرا اس ٹکڑے کے پاس پس اس کو کھا لیا تو شکار کھایا جائے گا اس لئے کہ اگر کتا اس حالت میں نفس شکار میں سے کھا لیتا تو اس کو مضر نہ ہوتا پس جبکہ اس نے وہ ٹکڑا کھا لیا جو شکار سے جدا ہے حالانکہ وہ اس کے مالک کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے تو بدرجہ اولی ( شکار حلال ہوگا ) ۔
تشریح یہ وہی پہلے والا مسئلہ ہے فرق اتنا ہے کہ پہلے کتا اس ٹکڑے کو کھانے میں مشغول ہو گیا تھا اور اس حالت میں کھایا نہیں بلکہ اس - کو پھینک کر شکار کا بدستور پیچھا کرتا رہا اور اس کو پکڑ لیا اور مار ڈالا تو اب اس کا کھانا حلال ہے اگر چہ مالک کے شکار کو لینے کے بعد سکتا اس ٹکڑے کو جا کر کھا لے تب بھی حلال ہے کیونکہ جب شکار مالک کے ہاتھوں میں آ گیا تو اب وہ شکار نہیں رہا یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر اس حالت میں کتنا مالک سے چھین کر بھی کھا لے تب بھی شکار حلال ہوتا ہے تو جب کتے نے وہ ٹکڑا کھایا جو مالک کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے تو یہ بدرجہ اولی شکار کی حلت کا باعث ہوگا۔ رہی پہلی حالت تو وہ اس لئے حلال نہیں تھا کہ کتے نے شکار کرنے کی حالت میں کھایا تھا جو اس کے جاہل ہونے کی دلیل تھی۔
بخلاف الوجه الأول لانه اكل فى حالة الاصطياد فكان جاهلا ممسكا لنفسه ولان نهس البضعة قد يكون ليا كلها وقد يكون حيلة فى الاصطياد ليضعف بقطع القطعة منه فيدركه فالا كل قبل الاخذ يدل على الوجه الاول وبعده على الوجه الثانى فلا يدل على جهله.
And if he threw away what he bit and followed the prey and killed it and did not eat from it, and his owner took it, then he passed by that piece and ate it, the prey is eaten (permissible) because if he had eaten from the prey itself in this state, it would not harm him; so when he ate what had separated from it, while it is not permissible for his owner, then all the more (the prey is permissible).
Translation: And if the dog threw away the piece he had bitten and chased the prey, then killed it and did not eat from it, and the owner took the prey, then the dog passed by that piece and ate it, then the prey will be eaten because if the dog had eaten from the prey itself in this state, it would not harm (the permissibility). So when he ate that separated piece, while it is not halal for its owner, then all the more (the prey is halal).
Commentary: This is the same issue as before, the difference is that in the first case the dog became engaged in eating that piece and in that state he ate, but in this case he spat it out and continued chasing the prey, caught it and killed it. So now its meat is halal. Even if after the owner took the prey, the dog goes and eats that piece, it is still halal because when the prey came into the owner's hands, it is no longer a prey. For this reason, if in this state the dog snatches from the owner and eats, even then the prey is halal. So when the dog ate that piece which is not halal for its owner, then all the more it will be a cause for the prey's permissibility. As for the first state, it was not halal because the dog ate during the hunting state, which was evidence of its ignorance.
Contrary to the first aspect because he ate in the state of hunting, so he was an ignorant dog holding for himself, and because biting the piece may be to eat it, and may be a trick in hunting to weaken the prey by cutting a piece from it so he can catch it. So eating before taking (the prey) indicates the first aspect, and after taking indicates the second aspect, so it does not indicate his ignorance.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two similar scenarios. In the first (previous lesson), the dog bit a piece, ate it during the chase, then killed the prey – that prey was haram because the dog showed ignorance. In this scenario, the dog bites a piece but then spits it out, continues the chase, kills the prey, and only later, after the owner has taken the prey, does the dog eat the separated piece. The ruling is that the prey is halal. The reasoning: if the dog had eaten from the prey itself after the owner's possession, it would not harm its permissibility (as established in the first lesson). So eating a detached piece, which is not even permitted for the owner to eat (because it is a detached part without proper slaughter), is even less harmful. The key difference is the timing: eating during the hunt (istiyad) indicates the dog is jahil (ignorant) because it prioritizes its own feeding over hunting. But biting and then spitting out the piece is not necessarily for eating; it could be a tactic to weaken the prey so it can be caught. Eating after the owner's possession does not reflect on the dog's training. Therefore, the prey is halal. The text also explains that the act of biting a piece can have two motives: (1) to eat it (indicates ignorance), or (2) to weaken the prey (does not indicate ignorance). The timing – before capturing (qabl al-akhdh) or after capturing (ba'dahu) – determines which motive is present. In this case, the dog did not eat the piece until after the owner possessed the prey, so the act is not evidence of ignorance.

Key Terms
اصطياد (istiyad): The act of hunting; the state when the dog is actively pursuing and capturing the prey.
حيلة (hilah): A trick or strategy; here, the dog biting a piece to weaken the prey, not necessarily to eat it.
جاهل (jahil): Ignorant; untrained. In hunting, a dog is considered jahil if it eats from the prey during the hunt, indicating it is not properly trained.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if a trained dog bites a piece from a live deer, spits it out, chases and kills the deer, and then after the hunter takes the deer, the dog eats that piece, what is the status of the deer meat?
A) Haram, because the dog consumed a part of the deer.
B) Halal, because the dog did not eat during the hunt and the act was a strategy.
C) Makruh, because the dog showed bad manners.
D) Only halal if the dog did not eat the piece at all.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of prey hunted by a trained dog depends on whether the dog eats from the prey during the hunt (istiyad) or after the owner's possession (ihraz); eating after possession does not invalidate the hunt.

Dog Eating Severed Piece After Capture Does Not Nullify Hunting
Explains ruling when dog eats severed piece after game is captured

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a hunting dog eats a severed piece after capture and explain the distinction from eating during the hunt.

Core Idea
A trained dog's eating after capture does not indicate jahalah; game remains halal.

This passage from Kitab al-Sayd addresses a nuanced scenario: a trained dog bites a piece from the game during the chase, drops it, continues hunting, kills the game, and later eats the severed piece after the hunter has taken it. The Hanafi ruling is that the game remains halal. The key distinction lies in the timing of the dog's eating—before or after capture—which indicates whether the dog was hunting for itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon. Here, it is the dog eating a severed piece after the hunter has taken the game. The ruling: the game is halal (permissible to eat).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is istihsan (juristic preference) based on the reasoning that if the dog had eaten from the game itself after capture, it would not nullify the hunt. Eating a separated piece is even less harmful.
The dalil is not a direct text but derived legal reasoning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The legal link: the dog's eating after capture does not show it was hunting for itself (jahalah). It may have bitten the piece as a trick (hilah) to weaken the prey. Thus, the hunting remains valid.
The text contrasts with a case where the dog eats during the hunt, which indicates jahalah and makes the game haram.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may consider any eating by the dog as nullifying the hunt. The Hanafi position distinguishes based on timing and intent.
The mukhtalaf fih status is recognized.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is based on the dog's training and the context of eating. Eating after capture does not undermine the dog's reliability as a trained hunter.
The mufta bihi is that the game is halal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصيد
کتے نے شکار پر حملہ کیا ایک عضو کاٹ لیا پھر شکار کا پیچھا کیا اور اس ٹکڑا کو نہیں کھایا یہ شکار کھانا حلال ہے ولو القى ما نهسه واتبع الصيد فقتله ولم ياكل منه واخذه صاحبه ثم مربتلك البضعة فاكلها يوكل الصيد لانه لواكل من نفس الصيد في هذه الحالة لن يضره فاذا اكل ما بان منه وهو لا يحل لصاحبه اولى
ترجمہ اور اگر کتے نے جو ٹکڑا نو چاہے اس کو ڈال دیا اور شکار کا پیچھا کیا پس اس کو قتل کر دیا اور اس میں سے نہیں کھایا اور شکار کو اس کے مالک نے لے لیا پھر سکتا گذرا اس ٹکڑے کے پاس پس اس کو کھا لیا تو شکار کھایا جائے گا اس لئے کہ اگر کتا اس حالت میں نفس شکار میں سے کھا لیتا تو اس کو مضر نہ ہوتا پس جبکہ اس نے وہ ٹکڑا کھا لیا جو شکار سے جدا ہے حالانکہ وہ اس کے مالک کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے تو بدرجہ اولی ( شکار حلال ہوگا ) ۔
تشریح یہ وہی پہلے والا مسئلہ ہے فرق اتنا ہے کہ پہلے کتا اس ٹکڑے کو کھانے میں مشغول ہو گیا تھا اور اس حالت میں کھایا نہیں بلکہ اس - کو پھینک کر شکار کا بدستور پیچھا کرتا رہا اور اس کو پکڑ لیا اور مار ڈالا تو اب اس کا کھانا حلال ہے اگر چہ مالک کے شکار کو لینے کے بعد سکتا اس ٹکڑے کو جا کر کھا لے تب بھی حلال ہے کیونکہ جب شکار مالک کے ہاتھوں میں آ گیا تو اب وہ شکار نہیں رہا یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر اس حالت میں کتنا مالک سے چھین کر بھی کھا لے تب بھی شکار حلال ہوتا ہے تو جب کتے نے وہ ٹکڑا کھایا جو مالک کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے تو یہ بدرجہ اولی شکار کی حلت کا باعث ہوگا۔ رہی پہلی حالت تو وہ اس لئے حلال نہیں تھا کہ کتے نے شکار کرنے کی حالت میں کھایا تھا جو اس کے جاہل ہونے کی دلیل تھی ۔
کتے نے ٹکڑا نوچ کر اس کو کھانا شروع کر دیا یہ اس کی جہالت کی دلیل ہے
بخلاف الوجه الأول لانه اكل فى حالة الاصطياد فكان جاهلا ممسكا لنفسه ولان نهس البضعة قد يكون ليا كلها وقد يكون حيلة فى الاصطياد ليضعف بقطع القطعة منه فيدركه فالا كل قبل الاخذ يدل على الوجه الاول وبعده على الوجه الثانى فلا يدل على جهله.
ترجمہ بخلاف پہلی صورت کے اس لئے کہ کتے نے شکار کرنے کی حالت میں کھایا ہے تو ہوگا یہ کتنا جاہل اپنے نفس کے لئے شکار و روکنے والا اور اس لئے کہ ٹکڑا نو چنا کبھی تو اس لئے ہوتا ہے کہ وہ اس کو کھائے اور کبھی شکار کرنے کا حیلہ ہوتا ہے، تا کہ شکار اس کا ٹکڑا کاتنے کی وجہ سے کمزور پڑ جائے پس وہ اس کو پکڑے تو شکار کو پکڑنے سے پہلے کھانا وجہ اول پر دال ہے ( کہ اس سے اپنے لئے کیا ہے تا کہ کھائے ) اور پکڑنے کے بعد ٹکڑا کھانا وجہ ثانی پر دال ہے ) کہ اس نے اس لئے کیا ہے تا کہ شکار کمزور پڑ جائے ) تو یہ کھانا اس کی جہالت پر دال نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اگر کتے نے ٹکڑا نوچ کر کھانا شروع کر دیا تھا تو یہ اس کی جہالت کی دلیل تھی لہذا اس شکار کا کھانا حلال نہیں ہے، اور نوچ کر نہ کھانا اور شکار کا پیچھا کرنا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اس نے یہ کام اس لئے کیا ہے کہ شکار کمزور پڑ جائے اور اس کے درد کی وجہ سے زیادہ نہ بھاگ سکے۔
تو پھر یہ فعل جہالت کی دلیل نہیں ہے لہذا اس کا کھانا حلال ہے، بہر حال کبھی ٹکڑے کو نو چنا کھانے کے لئے ہوتا ہے اور کبھی کمزور کرنے کے لئے تو جب اس نے کھانا شروع کر دیا تو وہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اس فعل کا مقصد یہی تھا لہذا معلوم ہوا کہ کتے نے
مالک کے لئے شکار نہیں کیا بلکہ اپنے لئے کیا ہے لہذا یہ حلال نہ ہوگا اور جب نہیں کھایا تو یہ اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ اس کے اس فعل کا مقصد شکار کو کمزور کرنا ہے لہذا اس کے کھانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
لہذا پکڑنے سے پہلے کھا ما وجہ اول پر دال ہے اور پکڑنے کے بعد کھانا دوسری صورت پر دال ہے تو یہ کھانا کتے کی جہالت پر دال
Kitab al-Sayd. A dog attacked the game, bit a limb, then chased the game and did not eat that piece; this game is halal to eat. And if he [the dog] dropped what he had bitten, followed the game, killed it, did not eat from it, and its owner took it, then later passed by that piece and ate it, the game is eaten because if he had eaten from the game itself in this state, it would not harm him. So if he ate what was separated from it, while it is not halal for its owner, it is more appropriate [that the game be halal]. Translation: 'And if the dog dropped the piece he had bitten...' Commentary: This is the same previous issue...
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning a dog that bites a piece from the game during the hunt, then drops it, continues chasing, kills the game, and later eats the severed piece after the hunter has taken the game. The ruling: the game is halal. The reasoning is that if the dog had eaten from the game itself in that situation (after capture), it would not nullify the hunting. Therefore, eating a piece that is already separated is even less harmful. The commentary contrasts this with a previous case where the dog ate the piece while still in the process of hunting, which indicated ignorance (jahalah) and made the game haram. Here, eating after capture shows the dog was not hunting for itself, so the game remains halal. The text also explains that biting a piece may be for eating or as a trick to weaken the prey; eating before capture indicates the first intent, after capture indicates the second.

Key Terms
بضعة (bughda): A piece or morsel of meat bitten off from the game.
جاهل (jahil): A dog that hunts for itself, indicating it is not properly trained.
حيلة (hilah): A trick or strategy used by the dog to weaken the game.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a dog bites a piece from the game, drops it, continues hunting, kills it, and later eats the piece after the hunter takes the game, is the game halal?
A) Yes, because the dog ate after capture, showing it was not hunting for itself.
B) No, because the dog ate a piece of the game.
C) Yes, but only if the piece was not eaten.
D) No, because the dog showed ignorance by biting before capture.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the game even if the dog later eats a severed piece, provided the dog did not eat during the hunt.

6 min
Requirement to Slaughter Game Found Alive After Hunting
States ruling: must slaughter game if found alive, or it becomes haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when game is found alive after hunting, explain the qiyas to tayammum, and apply the principle that regaining ability to perform the original act voids the substitute.

Core Idea
If the hunter can slaughter the game alive, he must; otherwise the substitute (hunting injury) becomes void and the meat is haram.

When hunting with trained animals or arrows, the game may be found alive. The Hanafi school holds that the hunter must then slaughter it ritually; otherwise, even if it dies from the wound, the meat is haram. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof through qiyas to the case of tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is finding the game alive after dispatching the dog, falcon, or arrow. The ruling is that the hunter must slaughter it; if he does not and it dies, the meat is not halal.
This is from the matn of al-Quduri.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to tayammum: if one finds water before praying, tayammum becomes void and wudu is obligatory. Similarly, if the hunter can slaughter (original) before the game dies from the wound (substitute), the substitute is void.
The analogy is explicit in the commentary.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The common element (illa) is the ability to perform the original act before the substitute achieves its purpose. In both cases, the purpose (permissibility of eating/validity of prayer) is not yet achieved, so the substitute is void.
The illa is the power over the original (al-qudra ala al-asl) before the purpose of the substitute is realized.
4
Note intra-madhhab nuance
The author added 'falcon and arrow' after the matn, but the commentator notes this is redundant because dispatching includes both, and arrow will be detailed later. This does not affect the ruling.
Redundancy is not an error.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence
If the hunter neglects to slaughter and the game dies, the meat is haram. This is the mufta bihi position.
There is no ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شکاری نے شکار پر اپنا کلب معلم یا معلم باز چھوڑایا تیر مارا جس سے شکار مرگیا تو کھانا حلال ہے اگر زندہ ہے تو ذبح سے حلال ہوگا
قال وان ادرك المرسل الصيد حيا وجب عليه ان يذكيه وان ترک تذكيته حتى مات لم يوكل وكذا البازي والسهم لانه قدر على الأصل قبل حصول المقصود بالبدل اذالمقصود هو الاباحة ولم تثبت قبل موته بطل حكم البدل
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر ارسال کرنے والے نے شکار کو زندہ پالیا تو اس پر واجب ہے کہ اس کو ذبح کرے اور اگر اس نے اس کے ذبح کرنے کو چھوڑ دیا یہاں تک کہ وہ مر گیا تو کھایا نہیں جائے گا اور ایسے ہی باز اور تیر اس لئے کہ وہ قادر ہو گیا ہے اصل کے اوپر مقصود کے حاصل ہونے سے پہلے بدل سے اس لئے کہ مقصود وہ اکل کی اباحت ہے اور اباحت ثابت نہ ہوگی شکار کی موت سے پہلے تو بدل کا حکم باطل ہو گیا۔ تشریح شکاری نے شکار پر اپنا کلب معلم یا معلم باز چھوڑ آیا تیر مارا جس سے شکار پکڑا گیا تو اب دیکھا جائے کہ وہ زندہ ہے یا مر گیا اگر مر گیا ہو تو اس کا کھانا حلال ہے۔ اور اگر زندہ ہو تو وہ جب حلال ہوگا کہ اس کو ذبح کر دیا جائے ورنہ اگر ذبح نہیں کیا گیا یہاں تک کہ وہ مرگیا تو حلال نہ ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ اصول یہ مقدر ہے اگر بدل سے مقصود کے حاصل ہونے سے پہلے پہلے اصل کے اوپر قدرت ہو جائے تو بدل کا حکم باطل ہو جاتا ہے مثلاً کسی نے تمیم کر لیا اور ابھی نماز نہیں پڑھی تھی کہ پانی پر قدرت ہوگئی تو حکم تیم باطل ہو گیا اور وضو کر کے نماز واجب ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح یہاں مقصود اکل کا مباح ہونا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اکل کی اباحت کا ظہور شکار کے مرنے کے بعد ہی ہوگا ورنہ اس کو زندہ کھانا حلال نہیں اور اصول ذکاۃ اختیاری ہے اور بدل ذکاۃ اضطراری ہے تو ذکاۃ اضطراری سے جو بدل ہے باطل ہو جائے گی۔ تنبیه و ان ادرک سے لم یو کل تک مختصر القدوری کی عبارت ہے اور وکذا البازی والسهم یہ مصنف کا اضافہ ہے مگر مصنف کا یہ اضافہ ایسا امرزائدہ ہے جس کی یہاں کوئی حاجت نہیں تھی تباز کے اضافہ درست نہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ارسال کلب اور باز دونوں کو شامل ہے ۔ ( کمال بھی ) اور ری کا اضافہ اس لئے صحیح نہیں کہ ری کا تفصیلی ذکر خود مستقل فصل میں آگے آرہا ہے بہر حال مصنف کا یہ اضافہ بر حل نہیں ہے كذافي نتائج الافكار.
A hunter dispatched his trained dog or trained falcon, or shot an arrow, and the game died: it is halal to eat; if it is alive, it becomes halal only by slaughter. He (al-Quduri) said: 'If the one who dispatched finds the game alive, he must slaughter it. If he leaves its slaughter until it dies, it is not eaten. Likewise the falcon and the arrow, because he has power over the original before the purpose is achieved by the substitute, since the purpose is permissibility of eating, and it is not established before its death, so the ruling of the substitute is void.' Translation: al-Quduri said... Commentary: The hunter dispatched his trained dog or trained falcon, or shot an arrow, and the game was caught. Now it is seen whether it is alive or dead. If dead, it is halal. If alive, it becomes halal only when he slaughters it. If he does not slaughter it until it dies, it is not halal. Because the principle is: if one gains power over the original before the purpose is achieved by the substitute, the substitute's ruling becomes void. For example, someone performed tayammum and had not yet prayed when he gained the ability to use water; then the ruling of tayammum becomes void and wudu and prayer become obligatory. Similarly here, the purpose is permissibility of eating, and it is clear that the permissibility of eating only appears after the death of the game; otherwise eating it alive is not halal, and the original is optional slaughter, while the substitute is compulsory slaughter, so the substitute by compulsory slaughter becomes void. Note: From 'wa in adraka' to 'lam yu'kal' is the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and 'wa kadha al-bazi wa al-sahm' is an addition by the author, but this addition is redundant; the addition of 'baz' is not correct because 'irsal' includes both dog and falcon, and the addition of 'ramy' is not correct because it will be detailed in a separate chapter later. However, this addition is not problematic. As in Nata'ij al-Afkar.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-madhhab note regarding the requirement to slaughter game that is found alive after being hunted by a trained dog, falcon, or arrow. The matn from al-Quduri states that if the hunter reaches the game alive, he must slaughter it; if he fails to do so and it dies, it is not halal. This applies to falcon and arrow as well. The proof is that the hunter has power over the original (optional slaughter) before the substitute (hunting injury) achieves its purpose (permissibility of eating). The analogy is drawn to tayammum: if one finds water before praying, tayammum is void. The commentary explains the ruling and notes that the addition of 'falcon and arrow' in the text is redundant but not incorrect, as dog and falcon are both included in the concept of dispatching, and arrow will be covered in its own chapter.

Key Terms
تذكية (tadhkiyah): Islamic ritual slaughter of an animal to make it halal.
بدل (badal): The substitute means of making meat halal (hunting injury) when the original (slaughter) is not possible.
اصل (asl): The original method of making meat halal, which is optional slaughter (al-dhakawat al-ikhtiyariyyah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunter dispatches a trained dog and finds the game alive, what must he do?
A) He must slaughter the game; otherwise it becomes haram if it dies.
B) He may leave it to die, and it will still be halal.
C) He must let the dog finish it off.
D) He must release the game back into the wild.

Key Takeaway
When a hunter finds game alive, he must slaughter it; otherwise the meat is haram, as the substitute (hunting injury) is void once the original (slaughter) becomes possible.

Obligation to Slaughter Game Found Alive
Ruling with proof from analogy to tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a hunter finds game alive and explain the Qiyas to Tayammum that nullifies the substitute method.

Core Idea
Ability to slaughter manually nullifies the substitute method.

This lesson examines a key ruling from the Kitab al-Sayd: when a hunter's trained animal or arrow strikes game but the animal remains alive, the hunter must slaughter it manually. The text justifies this ruling by a powerful analogy to tayammum, illustrating how the ability to perform the original act voids the substitute. We will walk through the ruling, its proof, and a brief note on the text's additions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate the core ruling: if the hunter finds the game alive, slaughter (dhabh) is wajib. If he abandons it until it dies, the meat is haram.
The ruling applies regardless of whether a dog, falcon, or arrow was used.
2
Distinguish the two methods of slaughter
Understand the concepts of dhakaah ikhtiyari (manual slaughter) and dhakaah idtirari (substitute via animal/arrow). The substitute is valid only when the hunter cannot perform original slaughter.
This is a distinctively Hanafi classification.
3
Trace the Qiyas to Tayammum
The text draws an analogy: just as tayammum is invalidated if water is found before prayer, the substitute slaughter is invalidated if the hunter can slaughter manually before the game dies.
The illa (effective cause) is 'ability over the original before attainment of purpose through substitute'.
4
Evaluate the author's addition
The commentator notes that the author's added phrase 'wa kadha al-bazi wa al-sahm' is redundant because the ruling already covers falcons, and arrows are treated separately.
This is a minor textual critique, not affecting the ruling's validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شکاری نے شکار پر اپنا کلب معلم یا معلم باز چھوڑایا تیر مارا جس سے شکار مرگیا تو کھانا حلال ہے اگر زندہ ہے تو ذبح سے حلال ہوگا
قال وان ادرك المرسل الصيد حيا وجب عليه ان يذكيه وان ترک تذكيته حتى مات لم يوكل وكذا البازي والسهم لانه قدر على الأصل قبل حصول المقصود بالبدل اذالمقصود هو الاباحة ولم تثبت قبل موته بطل حكم البدل
ترجمه قدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر ارسال کرنے والے نے شکار کو زندہ پالیا تو اس پر واجب ہے کہ اس کو ذبح کرے اور اگر اس نے اس کے ذبح کرنے کو چھوڑ دیا یہاں تک کہ وہ مر گیا تو کھایا نہیں جائے گا اور ایسے ہی باز اور تیر اس لئے کہ وہ قادر ہو گیا ہے اصل کے اوپر مقصود کے حاصل ہونے سے پہلے بدل سے اس لئے کہ مقصود وہ اکل کی اباحت ہے اور اباحت ثابت نہ ہوگی شکار کی موت سے پہلے تو بدل کا حکم باطل ہو گیا۔ تشریح شکاری نے شکار پر اپنا کلب معلم یا معلم باز چھوڑ آیا تیر مارا جس سے شکار پکڑا گیا تو اب دیکھا جائے کہ وہ زندہ ہے یا مر گیا اگر مر گیا ہو تو اس کا کھانا حلال ہے۔ اور اگر زندہ ہو تو وہ جب حلال ہوگا کہ اس کو ذبح کر دیا جائے ورنہ اگر ذبح نہیں کیا گیا یہاں تک کہ وہ مرگیا تو حلال نہ ہوگا۔
اس لئے کہ اصول یہ مقدر ہے اگر بدل سے مقصود کے حاصل ہونے سے پہلے پہلے اصل کے اوپر قدرت ہو جائے تو بدل کا حکم باطل ہو جاتا ہے مثلاً کسی نے تمیم کر لیا اور ابھی نماز نہیں پڑھی تھی کہ پانی پر قدرت ہوگئی تو حکم تیم باطل ہو گیا اور وضو کر کے نماز واجب ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح یہاں مقصود اکل کا مباح ہونا ہے اور ظاہر ہے کہ اکل کی اباحت کا ظہور شکار کے مرنے کے بعد ہی ہوگا ورنہ اس کو زندہ کھانا حلال نہیں اور اصول ذکاۃ اختیاری ہے اور بدل ذکاۃ اضطراری ہے تو ذکاۃ اضطراری سے جو بدل ہے باطل ہو جائے گی۔
تنبیه و ان ادرک سے لم یو کل تک مختصر القدوری کی عبارت ہے اور وکذا البازی والسهم یہ مصنف کا اضافہ ہے مگر مصنف کا یہ اضافہ ایسا امرزائدہ ہے جس کی یہاں کوئی حاجت نہیں تھی تباز کے اضافہ درست نہ ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ارسال کلب اور باز دونوں کو شامل ہے ۔ ( کمال بھی ) اور ری کا اضافہ اس لئے صحیح نہیں کہ ری کا تفصیلی ذکر خود مستقل فصل میں آگے آرہا ہے بہر حال مصنف کا یہ اضافہ بر حل نہیں ہے
كذافي نتائج الافكار.
The hunter released his trained dog or trained falcon, shot an arrow, and the game died, so eating is halal. If it is alive, then slaughter makes it halal. He (al-Quduri) said: If the sender found the game alive, it is obligatory upon him to slaughter it. If he abandoned slaughtering it until it died, it will not be eaten. Likewise the falcon and the arrow, because he became able (to slaughter) the original before the attainment of the intended purpose through the substitute, because the intended purpose is permission to eat, and permission is not established before its death, so the ruling of the substitute is nullified. Translation: al-Quduri said: And if the sender found the game alive, it is obligatory upon him to slaughter it, and if he abandoned slaughtering it until it died, it will not be eaten. Likewise the falcon and the arrow, because he became able over the original before attainment of the intended purpose through the substitute, because the intended purpose is permission to eat, and permission is not established before the death of the game, so the ruling of the substitute becomes nullified. Explanation: The hunter released his trained dog or trained falcon, shot an arrow, and the game was caught. Then it is seen whether it is alive or dead. If it is dead, eating it is halal. And if it is alive, it will be halal when he slaughters it. Otherwise, if he does not slaughter it until it dies, it will not be halal. Because the principle is that if one becomes able over the original before attaining the intended purpose through the substitute, the ruling of the substitute becomes nullified. For example, someone performed tayammum and had not yet prayed when he became able to use water, so the ruling of tayammum became nullified and he must perform wudu and pray. Similarly here, the intended purpose is permissibility of eating, and it is apparent that permissibility of eating appears only after the game dies, otherwise eating it alive is not halal. And the original slaughter is optional slaughter (ikhtiyari) and the substitute slaughter is compulsory slaughter (idtirari), so the substitute which is compulsory slaughter becomes nullified. Note: From 'wa in adraka' to 'lam yu'kal' is the text of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and 'wa kadha al-bazi wa al-sahm' is an addition by the author. But this addition by the author is an unnecessary thing; the reason the addition of 'baz' is not correct is that the sending of dog and falcon both are included. (Kamal also), and the addition of 'ramy' is not correct because the detailed mention of 'ramy' is coming later in a separate chapter. In any case, this addition by the author is not sound. So in Nata'ij al-Afkar.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Kitab al-Sayd. It states a key principle: when a hunter sends a trained dog or falcon, or shoots an arrow, and the game is found alive, the hunter must slaughter it. If he fails to do so and the game dies, it is not permissible to eat. The proof is a qiyas (analogy) to the case of tayammum: If a person performs tayammum but then finds water before starting prayer, the tayammum is nullified and he must perform wudu. Similarly, the substitute method of slaughter (by the dog/falcon/arrow) is only valid if the hunter cannot perform the original slaughter (dhabh ikhtiyari). Once he can slaughter, the substitute is invalid. The commentator also notes that the author's addition of 'wa kadha al-bazi wa al-sahm' is redundant; the sending of the falcon is already covered under the same ruling as the dog, and arrows will be discussed separately.

Key Terms
ذکاۃ اختیاری (dhakaah ikhtiyari): The prescribed, optional method of slaughter by cutting the throat (dhabh) when one has the ability to do so.
ذکاۃ اضطراری (dhakaah idtirari): The substitute method of slaughter via the wound inflicted by a trained dog, falcon, or arrow when the hunter cannot slaughter manually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a hunter finds the game alive after releasing a trained dog, and he has the ability to slaughter it but does not, and the game dies?
A) The game is halal because the dog's wound is sufficient.
B) The game is not halal because the substitute method is invalidated when the hunter can perform original slaughter.
C) The game is halal but the hunter must perform dam (expiation).
D) The game is halal only if the hunter had no knife.

Key Takeaway
If a hunter finds game alive and can slaughter, he must; otherwise the game becomes carrion.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Game Found Alive: Juridical Ability (Qudrah I'tibariyyah)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on game found alive when unable to slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding game found alive when the hunter cannot slaughter, and identify the mufta bihi position based on Zahir al-Riwayah.

Core Idea
Juridical ability (qudrah i'tibariyyah) makes the hunter responsible for slaughter even without a knife – the Zahir al-Riwayah position.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi dispute: when a hunter retrieves live game but cannot physically slaughter it (e.g., no knife), does its death render it halal or haram? The passage contrasts the relied-upon Zahir al-Riwayah position with the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and al-Shafi'i. Understanding the concept of juridical ability (qudrah i'tibariyyah) is key to grasping the Hanafi rule.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the Zahir al-Riwayah ruling
Identify the precise facts: hunter finds game alive, has possession but no ability to slaughter, game dies. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, the meat is not halal (haram).
2
Identify the opposing views
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (and al-Shafi'i) rule it halal. Their key evidence is the analogy (qiyas) to tayammum: if one sees water but cannot use it, tayammum remains valid.
This is the standard analogy (tashbih) used by the opposing school.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using juridical ability
Zahir al-Riwayah counters that once the hunter has possession of the game at the slaughter spot (the throat), he is considered able (qadir i'tibaran). This objective criterion avoids the variability of actual physical ability.
The key term is 'thabat yadahu ala al-madbah' – his hand is established on the slaughter spot.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in the same situation, a Hanafi following Zahir al-Riwayah cannot eat the meat; a Shafi'i (or Hanafi following the alternative view) can eat it.
This affects the hunter's behavior and legal responsibility.
5
Identify the tarjih (relied-upon position)
The text presents Zahir al-Riwayah as the mufta bihi. The opposing view is a minority within the Hanafi school and is not followed in fatwa.
Authority weight: zahir_riwayah (the six core books of Imam Muhammad).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شکاری نے شکار پایا ذبح پر قدرت کے باوجود ذبح نہ کیا اور شکار مر گیا تو کھانا حرام ہے
وهذا اذا تمكن من ذبحه اما اذا وقع في يده ولم يتمكن من ذبحه وفيه من الحيوة فوق ما يكون في المذبوح كل في ظاهر الرواية وعن ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف انه يحل وهو قول الشافعي لانه لم يقدر على الاصل صار كما اذارأى الماء ولم يقدر على تعمال ترجمہ اور یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ وہ ذبح پر قادر ہو جائے بہر حال جب شکار اس کے ہاتھ میں آیا اور وہ اس کے ذبح پر قادر نہیں ہے اور اس میں حیوۃ ہے مذبوح کی حیات سے زیادہ تو ظاہر الروایہ میں نہیں کھایا جائے گا اور ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ حلال ہے
اور یہی شافعی کا قول ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اصل پر قادر نہیں ہوا تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ جبکہ اس نے پانی کو دیکھا اور استعمال پر قادر نہیں ہوا۔ تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ حکم جو ہم نے بیان کیا ہے کہ اس کو کھانا حلال نہیں ہے یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ وہ شکار شکاری کو زندہ ملا ہو اور شکاری کو اس کے ذبح کرنے کی قدرت ہو پھر بھی اس نے ذبح نہ کیا ہو اور اگر قدرت نہ ہوئی ہو یا تو اس وجہ سے کہ چھری نہیں ہے یا چھری ہے لیکن اتنا وقت نہیں مل سکا کہ وہ چھری کو تیز کر کے اس کو ذبح کر سکے اس سے پہلے ہی وہ مر گیا تو اس کا حکم یہ نہیں ہے جو مذکور ہے بلکہ اس میں کچھ اختلاف ہے۔
اہر الروایہ تو یہ ہے کہ اگر ایسا ہوا مکہ اس کو وہ شکار زندہ ملا مگر اس کو کسی وجہ سے ذبح کی قدرت حاصل نہ ہوسکی نیہاں تک کہ وہ مر گیا تو اس کا کھانا حلال نہیں ہے اور یخین کی ایک روایت اور امام شافعی کا قول یہ ہے کہ وہ حلال ہے کیونکہ یہاں شکاری کو ذکاۃ اختیاری کی
قدرت حاصل ہی نہیں تو یہ تو ایسا ہے جیسے تیم نے پانی کو دیکھا اور استعمال پر قدرت نہ ہوئی تو اس کا تیم ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔ تنبیہ جانور کو ذبح کرنے کے بعد کچھ دیر تک اس میں کچھ حیات محسوس ہوتی ہے اگر شکار میں بھی اتنی حیات ہے تو یہ کالعدم ہے (کما سیاتی اور اگر اس سے زیادہ حیات ہو تب یہ اختلاف ہے جو مذکور ہوا۔ ظاہر الروایۃ کی دلیل
وجه الظاهر انه قدر اعتبارا لانه ثبت يده على المذبح وهو قائم مقام التمكن من الذبح اذلا يمكن اعتباره لانه لا بدله من مدة والناس يتفاوتون فيها على حسب تفاوتهم في الكياسة والهداية فى امر الذبح فادير الحكم على ما ذكرناه
ترجمہ ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ اعتباری لحاظ سے قادر ہو گیا اس لئے کہ اس کا قبضہ محل ذبح پر ثابت ہو چکا ہے اور یہ قبضہ ذبح پر قدرت کے قائم مقام ہے اس لئے کہ تمکن کا اعتبار ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ تمکن کے لئے کہ ایک مدت کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور لوگ اس مدت میں متفاوت ہوتے ہیں امر ذبح میں مہارت و ہدایت کے متفاوت ہونے کے اعتبار سے تو حکم کا مدار اسی پر ہوگا جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔
تشریح یہ ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حکمی اور اعتباری لحاظ سے شکاری کو ذبح پر قدرت حاصل ہو چکی ہے لیونکہ جب شکار اس کے ہاتھوں میں آ گیا تو محل ذبح اس کے ہاتھ میں آ گیا تو محل ذبح اس کے ہاتھ میں ہے اور یہ کل ذبح کا ہاتھوں
The hunter found the game; despite having power to slaughter, he did not slaughter and the game died, so eating is haram. This (ruling) is when he is able to slaughter. However, if it fell into his hand and he is not able to slaughter it, and there is life in it more than that in the slaughtered (animal) — according to Zahir al-Riwayah it is not eaten. And from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is halal, and that is the statement of al-Shafi'i, because he was not able over the original; it becomes like when he saw water and was not able to use it. Translation: This ruling is when he becomes able to slaughter. In any case, when the game came into his hand and he is not able to slaughter it, and there is life in it more than the life of a slaughtered animal, then according to Zahir al-Riwayah it will not be eaten, and from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf it is narrated that it is halal, and this is the statement of al-Shafi'i, because he was not able over the original, so it becomes like when he saw water and was not able to use it. Explanation: He says that this ruling which we mentioned, that eating it is not halal, is when the hunter found the game alive and he had the power to slaughter it yet did not. But if he did not have the power, either because there is no knife, or there is a knife but he could not get enough time to sharpen it and slaughter before it died, then the ruling is not as mentioned; rather there is some dispute. According to Zahir al-Riwayah, if such happened — that he found the game alive but for some reason could not get the power to slaughter until it died — then eating it is not halal. And one narration from Abu Yusuf and the statement of al-Shafi'i is that it is halal, because here the hunter had no power at all to perform optional slaughter (dhabh ikhtiyari), so this is like the one who performed tayammum after seeing water but was not able to use it — his tayammum does not become invalidated. Note: After slaughtering an animal, some life remains for a while. If the game also has that much life, it is disregarded (as will come later). If there is more life than that, then this dispute applies. The proof of Zahir al-Riwayah: The apparent reason is that he is considered able in a juridical sense because his hand is established on the place of slaughter, and this possession stands in place of ability to slaughter, because actual ability (tamakkun) cannot be considered due to the need for a certain duration, and people differ in that duration according to their difference in skill and guidance in the matter of slaughter. Therefore the ruling is based on what we have mentioned. Translation: The proof of Zahir al-Riwayah is that he became able in a juridical sense because his possession over the place of slaughter is established, and this possession stands in place of ability to slaughter, because actual ability cannot be considered; for ability, a certain period is necessary, and people differ in that period according to their difference in skill and guidance in the matter of slaughter. So the ruling depends on what we have mentioned. Explanation: This is the proof of Zahir al-Riwayah, the summary of which is that in a juridical and deeming sense, the hunter has obtained ability to slaughter, because when the game came into his hands, the place of slaughter came into his hands, and this possession is considered as equivalent to ability to slaughter.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The issue is: when a hunter finds the game alive but is unable to slaughter it (e.g., no knife, insufficient time), what is the ruling? According to Zahir al-Riwayah, it remains haram even if the hunter could not physically slaughter. The rationale is that the hunter's possession of the game at the slaughter spot (the throat) acts as a juridical (i'tibari) ability to slaughter. Since completely precise timing cannot be measured, the law uses this as a fixed criterion. On the other hand, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (and Imam al-Shafi'i) rule that it is halal, because the hunter genuinely lacked the ability to perform the original slaughter (dhabh ikhtiyari). They analogize to tayammum: if one sees water but cannot use it, his tayammum remains valid. Similarly, here the substitute method (by the dog or arrow) remains effective.

Key Terms
ظاہر الروایہ (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted and authoritative rulings from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Represents the dominant position in the Hanafi school.
قدرة اعتبارية (qudrah i'tibariyyah): Juridical or deeming ability: the law considers the hunter able to slaughter simply because he has control of the game's slaughter place, regardless of actual physical ability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling if a hunter finds a game alive but has no knife to slaughter it, and it dies?
A) It is halal because he was unable to slaughter.
B) It is not halal because he is considered able once he has possession of the game.
C) It is halal only if the dog or falcon caused the death.
D) It is halal unconditionally.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, juridical ability (qudrah i'tibariyyah) based on possession of the game at the slaughter spot makes the hunter responsible for slaughter; failure renders the meat haram according to Zahir al-Riwayah.

Ruling on Game That Dies Before Slaughter: Constructive Ability
Ruling on game that dies before slaughter with conditions and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on game that dies before slaughter when the hunter lacks actual ability, and explain the proof based on constructive ability (qudra i'tibariyya).

Core Idea
Game that dies in the hunter's hand is haram because constructive ability exists, even if actual slaughter was impossible.

This lesson tackles a common hunter's dilemma: a game animal is caught alive but dies before the hunter can slaughter it. The ruling hinges on whether the hunter had any form of ability to slaughter, even if actual slaughter was impossible. We will explore the Hanafi position, its proof, and the disagreement with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act? A hunted animal caught alive dies before the hunter slaughters it. The ruling in the Hanafi school: it is haram to eat when the hunter had constructive ability.
Constructive ability means the animal was in the hunter's hand, giving him control over the place of slaughter.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, there is a narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that it is halal, using qiyas with tayammum. The zahir al-riwayah (relied-upon position) holds it haram.
Imam Muhammad's view is the basis of zahir al-riwayah.
3
Identify the opposing school
Imam al-Shafi'i agrees with the halal narration, analogizing to the case of seeing water but being unable to use it.
Shafi'i position: if the hunter cannot perform optional slaughter, the game remains in its original state and dharuri slaughter suffices.
4
Trace the Hanafi proof
The proof for the haram position is qiyas: once the animal is in the hunter's hand, he has constructive ability because his hand is on the place of slaughter. This is a jaliyyah (obvious) illa. Actual ability varies and cannot be measured objectively.
The text states: 'his hand was established on the place of slaughter, and that takes the place of ability to slaughter'.
5
Determine practical consequence
In practice, the mufta bihi is that the meat is haram. The Shafi'i school considers it halal. This difference affects how hunters should handle game that dies before slaughter.
Important exception: if the animal has only twitching life (like a normally slaughtered animal), it is considered dead and the first wound suffices. That is halal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شکاری نے شکار پایا ذبح پر قدرت کے باوجود ذبح نہ کیا اور شکار مر گیا تو کھانا حرام ہے

وهذا اذا تمكن من ذبحه اما اذا وقع في يده ولم يتمكن من ذبحه وفيه من الحيوة فوق ما يكون في المذبوح كل في ظاهر الرواية وعن ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف انه يحل وهو قول الشافعي لانه لم يقدر على الاصل صار كما إذا رأى الماء ولم يقدر على استعماله

ترجمہ اور یہ حکم اس وقت ہے جبکہ وہ ذبح پر قادر ہو جائے بہر حال جب شکار اس کے ہاتھ میں آیا اور وہ اس کے ذبح پر قادر نہیں ہے اور اس میں حیوۃ ہے مذبوح کی حیات سے زیادہ تو ظاہر الروایہ میں نہیں کھایا جائے گا اور ابو حنیفہ اور ابو یوسف سے منقول ہے کہ حلال ہے اور یہی شافعی کا قول ہے اس لئے کہ وہ اصل پر قادر نہیں ہوا تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ جبکہ اس نے پانی کو دیکھا اور استعمال پر قادر نہیں ہوا۔

تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ حکم جو ہم نے بیان کیا ہے کہ اس کو کھانا حلال نہیں ہے یہ اس وقت ہے جبکہ وہ شکار شکاری کو زندہ ملا ہو اور شکاری کو اس کے ذبح کرنے کی قدرت ہو پھر بھی اس نے ذبح نہ کیا ہو اور اگر قدرت نہ ہوئی ہو یا تو اس وجہ سے کہ چھری نہیں ہے یا چھری ہے لیکن اتنا وقت نہیں مل سکا کہ وہ چھری کو تیز کر کے اس کو ذبح کر سکے اس سے پہلے ہی وہ مر گیا تو اس کا حکم یہ نہیں ہے جو مذکور ہے بلکہ اس میں کچھ اختلاف ہے۔

ظاہر الروایہ تو یہ ہے کہ اگر ایسا ہوا کہ اس کو وہ شکار زندہ ملا مگر اس کو کسی وجہ سے ذبح کی قدرت حاصل نہ ہوسکی یہاں تک کہ وہ مر گیا تو اس کا کھانا حلال نہیں ہے اور دوسری ایک روایت اور امام شافعی کا قول یہ ہے کہ وہ حلال ہے کیونکہ یہاں شکاری کو ذکاۃ اختیاری کی قدرت حاصل ہی نہیں تو یہ تو ایسا ہے جیسے تیمم نے پانی کو دیکھا اور استعمال پر قدرت نہ ہوئی تو اس کا تیمم ساقط نہیں ہوتا۔

تنبیہ جانور کو ذبح کرنے کے بعد کچھ دیر تک اس میں کچھ حیات محسوس ہوتی ہے اگر شکار میں بھی اتنی حیات ہے تو یہ کالعدم ہے (کما سیاتی) اور اگر اس سے زیادہ حیات ہو تب یہ اختلاف ہے جو مذکور ہوا۔

ظاہر الروایۃ کی دلیل

وجه الظاهر انه قدر اعتبارا لانه ثبت يده على المذبح وهو قائم مقام التمكن من الذبح اذ لا يمكن اعتباره لانه لا بد له من مدة والناس يتفاوتون فيها على حسب تفاوتهم في الكياسة والهداية فى امر الذبح فادير الحكم على ما ذكرناه

ترجمہ ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وہ اعتباری لحاظ سے قادر ہو گیا اس لئے کہ اس کا قبضہ محل ذبح پر ثابت ہو چکا ہے اور یہ قبضہ ذبح پر قدرت کے قائم مقام ہے اس لئے کہ تمکن کا اعتبار ممکن نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ تمکن کے لئے ایک مدت کا ہونا ضروری ہے اور لوگ اس مدت میں متفاوت ہوتے ہیں امر ذبح میں مہارت و ہدایت کے متفاوت ہونے کے اعتبار سے تو حکم کا مدار اسی پر ہوگا جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں۔

تشریح یہ ظاہر الروایہ کی دلیل ہے جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ حکمی اور اعتباری لحاظ سے شکاری کو ذبح پر قدرت حاصل ہو چکی ہے کیونکہ جب شکار اس کے ہاتھوں میں آ گیا تو محل ذبح اس کے ہاتھ میں آ گیا تو محل ذبح اس کے ہاتھ میں ہے اور یہ کہ ذبح کا ہاتھوں میں ہونا ذبح پر قدرت کے قائم مقام ہے اس لئے کہ حقیقی تمکن کا اعتبار تو مشکل معاملہ ہے اس لئے کہ اس کے لئے پھر ایک مدت درکار ہوگی۔ پھر وہ مدت کتنی ہو یہ بھاری مسئلہ ہوگا کیونکہ ذبح کے معاملہ میں لوگ متفاوت ہیں کوئی جلدی ذبح کر دیتا ہے کہ اس کو مہارت و سلیقہ اور تجربہ ہے بعض لوگ اناڑی ہوتے ہیں کہ اس میں بہت دیر لگا دیں تو بس قدرت و تمکن کا مدار اس پر رہا کہ اس کے ہاتھوں میں شکار آ جائے۔

شکار میں اتنی حیات ہے جتنی مذبوح میں تو اسے حیات نہیں کہیں گے

بخلاف ما اذا بقى فيه من الحيوة مثل ما يبقى في المذبوح لانه ميت حكما الاترى انه لو وقع فى الماء وهو بهذه الحالة لم يحرم كما اذا وقع وهو ميت والميت ليس بمذبح

ترجمہ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ شکار میں اتنی حیات باقی ہو جتنی مذبوح میں باقی رہتی ہے اس لئے کہ وہ حکما میت ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر شکار پانی میں گر جائے اور وہ اسی حالت پر ہو تو حرام نہیں ہوتا جیسا کہ شکار پانی میں گر جائے حالانکہ وہ میت ہو اور میت ذبح کا محل نہیں ہے۔

تشریح جس شکار سے بحث چل رہی ہے اگر اس کی پوزیشن یہ ہو کہ اس میں حیات ہے مگر وہ حیات اتنی ہے جتنی مذبوح میں ہوتی ہے تو اسے حیات نہیں کہیں گے بلکہ یہ تو اضطراب کی وجہ سے گوشت کی پھٹک ہے اس کو ذبح کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں کیونکہ وہ تو مرا ہوا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر وہ اس حالت میں پانی میں گر جائے اور اس میں صرف اتنی حیات ہو جتنی مذبوح میں ہوتی ہے تو وہ حرام نہیں ہوگا جیسا کہ اگر بالکل مرا ہوا شکار یا مذبوح پانی میں گر جائے تو وہ حرام نہ ہوگا اور میت ذبح کا محل نہیں ہوتا لہذا اس کو ذبح نہیں کیا جائے گا اور پہلی ذکاۃ اضطراری اس کے حلال ہونے کے لئے کافی ہوگی۔

شکار میں حیات ہو اور مذبوح کی حیات سے زیادہ ہو ذبح پر قدرت ہونے یا نہ ہونے کا حکم

وفصل بعضهم فيه تفصيلا وهو انه ان لم يتمكن لفقد الألة لم يوكل وان لم يتمكن لضيق الوقت لم يوكل عندنا خلافا للشافعي لانه اذا وقع فى يده لم يبق صيدا فبطل حكم ذكاة الاضطرار وهذا اذا كان يتوهم بقاؤه

ترجمہ اور بعض مشائخ نے اس میں (جبکہ شکار میں مذبوح سے زیادہ حیات ہو) کچھ تفصیل کی ہے اور وہ یہ ہے کہ اگر وہ قادر نہ ہو آلہ کے مفقود ہونے کی وجہ سے تو نہیں کھایا جائے گا اور اگر قادر نہ ہو وقت کی تنگی کی وجہ سے تو ہمارے نزدیک نہیں کھایا جائے گا اختلاف ہے امام شافعی کا (ہماری دلیل یہ ہے) اس لئے کہ شکار جب اس کے ہاتھ میں آ گیا تو شکار نہیں رہا تو ذکاۃ اضطراری کا حکم باطل ہو گیا اور یہ (عدم حلت) جب ہے جب کہ اس کی بقاء کا توہم ہو۔

تشریح بعض مشائخ نے اس کی یہ تفصیل بیان کی ہے کہ اگر شکار میں حیات ہے اور وہ حیات مذبوح کی حیات سے زیادہ ہے اسے دیکھا جائے کہ ذبح پر قدرت کیوں نہیں اگر چھری وغیرہ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے قدرت نہیں تو اس کا کھانا حلال نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ کوتاہی شکاری کی طرف سے ہے کہ اس نے چھری کو کیوں ساتھ نہیں رکھا۔ اور اگر قدرت نہ ہونے کا سبب وقت کی تنگی ہے تو بھی ہمارے نزدیک نہیں کھایا جائے گا امام شافعی کے نزدیک وہ حلال ہے اور یہ استحسان ہے اور یہی حسن بن زیاد اور محمد بن مقاتل کا قول ہے اور قاضی خان
The hunter found the game and did not slaughter despite ability, and the game died, so eating it is prohibited. This is when he is able to slaughter it. But if it fell into his hand and he was unable to slaughter it, and it has life above that which is in a slaughtered animal, then in zahir al-riwayah it is not eaten, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that it is permissible, and that is the saying of al-Shafi'i, because he was not able to perform the original (slaughter), so it became like when he sees water but is unable to use it. Translation: This ruling is when he becomes able to slaughter. However, when the game came into his hand and he is not able to slaughter it, and it has life more than the life of a slaughtered animal, then in zahir al-riwayah it will not be eaten, and it is narrated from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that it is permissible, and this is the saying of al-Shafi'i, because he was not able to perform the original, so it became like when he saw water and was unable to use it. Explanation: They say that this ruling which we mentioned, that eating it is not permissible, is when the hunter found the game alive and the hunter had ability to slaughter it but still did not slaughter. And if he did not have ability, either because there is no knife, or there is a knife but he could not get enough time to sharpen it and slaughter it before it died, then its ruling is not what was mentioned, rather there is some difference. Zahir al-riwayah is that if it happened that he found the game alive but for some reason could not obtain ability to slaughter until it died, then eating it is not permissible. And another narration and the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i is that it is permissible, because here the hunter does not have ability for optional slaughter at all, so this is like someone who sees water but is unable to use it, then his tayammum is not invalidated. Note: After slaughtering an animal, some life is felt in it for a while. If the game also has that much life, then it is negligible (as will come). And if there is more life than that, then this difference occurs as mentioned. The proof of zahir al-riwayah: The apparent face is that he became able in a constructive sense because his hand was established on the place of slaughter, and that takes the place of ability to slaughter, because actual ability cannot be considered, as it requires a duration, and people differ in that duration according to their difference in skill and guidance in the matter of slaughter. So the ruling is based on what we mentioned. Translation: The proof of zahir al-riwayah is that he became able in a constructive sense because his possession of the place of slaughter is established, and this possession takes the place of ability to slaughter, because actual ability cannot be considered, because ability requires a duration, and people differ in that duration according to their difference in skill and guidance in the matter of slaughter, so the ruling will be based on what we mentioned. Explanation: This is the proof of zahir al-riwayah, the gist of which is that in a legal and constructive sense, the hunter has obtained ability to slaughter, because when the game came into his hands, the place of slaughter came into his hands, and having the place of slaughter in his hands takes the place of ability to slaughter, because actual ability is a difficult matter, as it requires a duration. Then how long that duration is is a heavy issue, because people differ in the matter of slaughter; some slaughter quickly because they have skill and experience, some are clumsy and take a long time. So ability and control are based on the game coming into his hands. If the game has as much life as a slaughtered animal, then it is not considered life. Contrary to the case when there remains in it life similar to that which remains in a slaughtered animal, because it is legally dead. Do you not see that if it falls into water in this state, it is not prohibited, just as if it falls and is dead, and a dead animal is not a place for slaughter. Translation: Contrary to the case when the game has as much life remaining as remains in a slaughtered animal, because it is legally dead. Do you not see that if the game falls into water and it is in this state, it is not prohibited, just as if the game falls into water while it is dead, and a dead animal is not a place for slaughter. Explanation: The game under discussion, if its condition is that it has life but that life is as much as is in a slaughtered animal, then it will not be called life; rather it is just twitching of meat due to agitation. There is no need to slaughter it because it is dead. This is why if it falls into water in this state and it has only that much life, it will not be prohibited, just as if a completely dead game or slaughtered animal falls into water, it will not be prohibited. And a dead animal is not a place for slaughter, so it will not be slaughtered, and the first dharuri slaughter will be sufficient for its permissibility. The ruling when the game has life and that life is more than the life of a slaughtered animal, and there is or is not ability to slaughter. Some scholars detailed it: If he was unable due to lack of a tool, it is not eaten. And if he was unable due to lack of time, it is not eaten according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because when it fell into his hand, it is no longer game, so the ruling of dharuri slaughter is invalidated. And this (impermissibility) is when its survival is speculated. Translation: Some scholars gave a detail in this (when the game has more life than a slaughtered animal): If he is unable due to the lack of a tool, it will not be eaten. And if he is unable due to lack of time, then according to us it will not be eaten, there is a difference with Imam al-Shafi'i (our proof is) because when the game came into his hand, it is no longer game, so the ruling of dharuri slaughter is invalidated. And this (impermissibility) is when its survival is speculated. Explanation: Some scholars gave this detail: If the game has life and that life is more than the life of a slaughtered animal, then see why he is unable to slaughter. If he is unable due to the lack of a knife etc., then it will not be permissible to eat, because the negligence is from the hunter for not keeping a knife with him. And if the reason for inability is lack of time, then also according to us it will not be eaten. Imam al-Shafi'i considers it permissible. And this is istihsan, and this is the saying of Hasan ibn Ziyad and Muhammad ibn Muqatil, and Qadi Khan.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Sayd deals with the ruling on game that a hunter catches alive but dies before being slaughtered. The passage is a ruling with proof, including an intra-Hanafi dispute and an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. The main ruling is stated first: if the hunter has the ability to slaughter but does not, the meat is haram. The focus then shifts to the case where the hunter lacks ability—either because he has no tool or because time is insufficient. In the zahir al-riwayah (the relied-upon transmission from Imam Muhammad), if the animal has more life than a normally slaughtered animal, it is not permissible to eat. However, a narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, also held by al-Shafi'i, says it is halal, drawing an analogy to tayammum when water is seen but cannot be used. The passage then presents the proof for the zahir al-riwayah position: once the hunter has the animal in hand, he is considered to have constructive ability (qudra i'tibariyya) to slaughter, because his hand is on the place of slaughter. Actual ability is not required because it would vary between people, making the law uncertain. The text further distinguishes the amount of life: if the animal has only as much life as a slaughtered animal (twitching), it is legally dead and does not require a second slaughter; the initial hunting (dharuri slaughter) suffices. If it has more life than that, the dispute applies. Finally, some later scholars (mashayikh) give a further detail: if the inability is due to a missing tool, the meat is haram because the hunter was negligent; if due to shortness of time, it is also haram according to the Hanafi school, but al-Shafi'i considers it halal. This last detail is reported as istihsan from Hasan ibn Ziyad and Muhammad ibn Muqatil.

Key Terms
ذكاة اضطراري (dhakāt iḍṭirārī): Slaughter performed in necessity, such as when a hunter catches game and slaughters it without formal conditions; also the initial wound from hunting is considered dharuri slaughter.
قدر اعتباري (qudra iʿtibāriyya): Constructive or legal ability; the ability attributed to a person by law, here based on possession of the animal's slaughter place.
تمكن (tamakkun): Actual ability or control to perform an act, requiring both means and time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the zahir al-riwayah, if a hunter catches a game animal alive but has no knife and the animal dies, what is the ruling on eating it?
A) It is halal because the hunter had no ability to slaughter.
B) It is haram because the hunter had constructive ability once the animal was in his hand.
C) It is disliked (makruh) but permissible if necessary.
D) It is halal only if the animal had life less than a slaughtered animal.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, game that dies in the hunter's hand is haram because constructive ability is established, even if actual slaughter was impossible.

The Ruling on a Hunted Animal with Only Convulsive Movements
Ruling that an animal with only convulsive movements is already dead

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a hunted animal that shows only convulsive movements and explain the analogical proof (qiyas) that supports it.

Core Idea
If a hunted animal has only the convulsive movements of a slaughtered animal, it is legally dead and halal without further slaughter.

In hunting, a question arises: if you wound an animal and find it motionless except for minor twitching, must you still slaughter it? The Hanafi school addresses this with a clear ruling based on the concept of legal death (mawt hukmi). This lesson unpacks the proof, which relies on qiyas with a slaughtered animal falling into water.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The subject is a hunted animal that, when reached, has only the same level of life as a properly slaughtered animal (i.e., convulsive movements). The ruling is that this animal is legally dead and permissible (halal) without any additional slaughter.
2
Understand the key distinction
The 'life' observed is not genuine life (hayat haqiqiyyah) but mere muscular convulsions (harakat al-idtirab) that occur after death. The Hanafi school considers this legally equivalent to death.
This distinction is crucial: true life would require slaughter.
3
Analyze the proof (qiyas)
The passage uses analogy (qiyas) with a slaughtered animal that falls into water: just as a slaughtered animal does not become unlawful by falling into water, so too does a hunted animal in the same condition (legally dead) remain lawful.
The shared attribute (illa) is legal death (mawt hukmi).
4
Note the legal consequence
Because the animal is legally dead, there is no need for slaughter. The initial hunting wound (dhakaat al-idadtirari) is sufficient for permissibility.
If the animal had genuine life, the ruling would be different.

شکار میں اتنی حیات ہے جتنی مذبوح میںتو اسے حیات نہیں کہیں گے بخلاف ما اذا بقى فيه من الحيوة مثل ما يبقى في المذبوح لانه ميت حكما الاترى انه لو وقع فى الماء وهو بهذه الحالة لم : يحرم م كما اذا وقع وهو ميت والميت ليس بمذبح ترجمه بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ شکار میں اتنی حیات باقی ہو جتنی مذبوح میں باقی رہتی ہے اس لئے کہ وہ حکمامیت ہے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ اگر شکار پانی میں گر جائے اور وہ اسی حالت پر ہو تو حرام نہیں ہوتا جیسا کہ شکار پانی میں گر جائے حالانکہ وہ میت ہو اور میت ذبح کا محل نہیں ہے۔ تشریح جس شکار سے بحث چل رہی ہے اگر اس کی پوزیشن یہ ہو کہ اس میں حیات ہے مگر وہ حیات اتنی ہے جتنی مذبوح میں ہوتی ہے تو اسکو حیات نہیں کہیں گے بلکہ یہ تو اضطراب کی وجہ سے گوشت کی پھٹک ہے اس کو ذبح کرنے کی ضرورت نہیں کیونکہ وہ تو مرا ہوا ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر وہ اس حالت میں پانی میں گر جائے اور اس میں صرف اتنی حیات ہو جتنی مذبوح میں ہوتی ہے تو وہ حرام نہیں ہوگا جیسا کہ اگر بالکل مرا ہوا شکار یا منذ بوح پانی میں گر جائے تو وہ حرام نہ ہوگا اور میت ذبح کا محل نہیں ہوتا لہذا اس کو ذبح نہیں کیا جائے گا اور پہلی ذکاۃ اضطراری اس کے حلال ہونے کے لئے کافی ہوگی۔
If the game has as much life as a slaughtered animal, then it is not considered alive. Contrary to if there remains in it life like that which remains in a slaughtered animal, because it is legally dead. Do you not see that if it falls into water in this state, it is not unlawful? Just as if it fell while dead. And a dead animal is not a place for slaughter. Translation: Contrary to the case where so much life remains in the game as remains in a slaughtered animal, because it is legally dead. Do you not see that if the game falls into water in that state, it does not become unlawful? Just as if the game falls into water while dead. And a dead animal is not a place for slaughter. Commentary: The game under discussion, if its condition is such that it has life but that life is as much as in a slaughtered animal, then it will not be called life; rather, it is the convulsion of meat due to agitation. There is no need to slaughter it because it is already dead. This is why if it falls into water in that state and has only as much life as in a slaughtered animal, it will not become unlawful. Just as if a completely dead game or slaughtered animal falls into water, it does not become unlawful. And a dead animal is not a place for slaughter. Therefore, it will not be slaughtered, and the first emergency slaughter (dhakaat al-idadtirari) will be sufficient for its permissibility.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding a hunted animal that has only the same level of life as an animal that has been properly slaughtered. The ruling is that such an animal is legally considered dead, and therefore it is permissible to eat without additional slaughter. The proof is analogical: just as a slaughtered animal that falls into water remains lawful, so too does a hunted animal in a comparable state. The commentary clarifies that the observed movement in such an animal is not genuine life but mere muscular convulsion (اضطراب). Hence, the initial wound from hunting is sufficient to render it halal.

Key Terms
ذکاۃ اضطراری (dhakaat al-idadtirari): The initial wound by hunting that substitutes for slaughter in case of emergency when actual slaughter is impossible.
مذبوح (madhbuh): An animal that has been properly slaughtered according to Islamic law.
حیات (hayat): Life as a legal condition for requiring slaughter; the convulsive movements after death are not considered true life.
